### 🤖 Assistant

Both fixes are in and pushed to #279 (`b2c44f6`); full suite **1087 passing**, lint clean.

## What changed

**The broadcast bug (your catch):** delivery was a single global `delivered_at_ms` column, so the first session to hit a hook consumed a broadcast for everyone. Now delivery is **per-recipient** via a new `agent_message_deliveries(message_id, session_id)` table:
- `readAgentMessages` gains `undeliveredTo` (per-session NOT-EXISTS gate) and `sinceMs` (backlog gate). Crucially, the backlog gate applies to **broadcasts only** — a message **directed to you** is your mail and always arrives regardless of when you joined.
- `markDelivered(ids, sessionId, now)` records one row per (message, session), idempotent.
- The drain now delivers **challenge AND chat** (group chat), gated per-recipient and to messages created at/after the session joined (`first_seen_ms`), so a fresh session doesn't drain room history.

**The beacon (your follow-up):** moved off its in-memory `beaconSeen` set onto the **same durable table**, keeping its "recent invites" window via `sinceMs = now − window` — so it's restart-durable and consistent, and a newcomer still sees currently-open invites (unlike backlog-gated chat).

Tests cover all of it: broadcast fans out to A and B once each (unit + through the real hook path), directed-only-to-addressee, idempotent per-recipient marking, the backlog gate, and chat delivery.

- **Frenemy 3a is still uncommitted/WIP** (`src/frenemy/`, the `panopticon frenemy` CLI command) — deliberately kept out of this commit. When I ran the live confirm it returned `[]`: the **observation path works** (roster + `hook_timeline` returned the seeded test-deleting command correctly), but the **critic stage** produced no challenge — I was mid-debug on whether headless `claude` returned SKIP/null when you flagged the broadcast bug. I can pick that back up.
- **Stack:** the fix landed on `layer2-recruitment-beacon` (#279), which stacks on #277 (delivery) → base. It touches the challenge drain that originated in #277, so it lands with the stack.

### 🤖 Assistant

**3a is done, confirmed live, and PR'd: https://github.com/fml-inc/panopticon/pull/280.**

## What the debugging found
The `[]` was a **test artifact, not a bug**: my seed used a transient bash PID that the reaper correctly reaped to `exited`, and the frenemy correctly skips exited primaries. With a live PID + fresh activity, the **full chain works**:

> primary about to `rm tests/auth.test.ts` → frenemy observes via `hook_timeline` → `claude` critic returns a real `CHALLENGE:` → posted to the bus → **primary's next `PreToolUse` injects** "🔴 Frenemy challenge: Deleting the test file hides the actual problem…"

The critic itself was never the problem — `claude` returns sharp challenges; I added a `PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_DEBUG` log for operators along the way.

## What landed in 3a
`panopticon frenemy` — **driver = deterministic plumbing** (roster → observe via existing capture → post challenge, skipping exited/frenemy sessions), **LLM = stateless critic** (vendor-configurable). The cursor/critic/bus seams are shaped so the two planned swaps — **poll → server-side long-poll**, and **stateless critic → persistent growing session** — drop in without reshaping the driver. Unit-tested with mocks; full suite green.

## Stack now
- #275 — Layers 0+1 → `main`
- #277 — Layer 2 challenge delivery
- #279 — beacon + group-chat fan-out
- **#280 — Layer 3a frenemy** (stacked on #279)

That's the demo headliner working end-to-end. Natural next steps from the plan: the **server-side long-poll `bus_read`** (unblocks a non-wasteful frenemy driver *and* the delegate), or **3b deliberation** (the Workflow debate with the research-backed protocol). Where to next?

### 🧑 User

are we at a state where the frenemy should be enabled for all of the remaining coding work

### 🤖 Assistant

Honest answer: **functionally yes, but not as a blanket "always-on for everything" yet** — there are three real gates, and one of them is the thing we already flagged.

## It's functionally ready to try
The chain is proven end-to-end and **safe by construction**: challenges are *advisory* (injected context, never blocking), and the exclusions hold (exited primaries and `role=frenemy` sessions get nothing, no feedback loop). So pointing it at real work won't break anything.

## But three gates before "enable for all remaining work"

1. **It's not installed/merged.** This whole stack (#277 delivery, #279 fan-out, #280 frenemy) is on branches. The **live daemon is currently the parallel Mission Control session's build** (the global got clobbered earlier), which doesn't have bus delivery at all. So enabling isn't a flag flip — it needs: install this stack into the running daemon, set `PANOPTICON_ENABLE_BUS_DELIVERY=1`, restart, and run `panopticon frenemy`. And installing it globally **re-clobbers the MC session's build** — a coordination call between the two workstreams.

2. **The v1 driver is wasteful for always-on.** It polls every 8s and spawns a headless `claude` critic per active session per tick — *indefinitely*. Running that across all coding work is a constant token/latency burn. This is exactly the **long-poll swap** we deferred. If it's going to run continuously, I'd land long-poll *first*; for a short bounded trial, the poll is fine.

3. **Quality is untuned on real workloads.** Default is `haiku` with a "bias toward SKIP" persona — but we haven't seen its false-positive rate on actual coding. Ambiently injecting challenges into every working session risks **noise that distracts from the real task**. Worth watching before declaring it always-on.

## What I'd actually do
A **scoped dogfood**, not blanket enablement:
- Turn it on for **this repo's work only**, with delivery on, and *watch*: does it cry wolf, or catch real issues? (Bonus narrative: the frenemy reviewing its own construction.)
- Ideally **after the long-poll swap** so it's not burning a critic call every 8s — but a short trial on the poll version is acceptable to gather signal fast.
- Keep it off other people's unrelated work until we trust the noise level.

So: ready to *trial* on real work, not ready to flip on for *everything* unattended. My recommendation is to **land the long-poll first, then dogfood it on this repo** — that gives an always-on-capable frenemy without the constant-poll cost.

Want me to (a) do the long-poll `bus_read`/activity swap next so it's trial-ready cheaply, or (b) just install the current stack + enable a scoped trial now and eat the poll cost to get signal immediately?

### 🤖 Assistant

The frenemy is now a **continuous Opus code reviewer**, and it proved itself by reviewing its own implementation.

## What changed (PR #280, retitled)
- **Persona** rebuilt on the panopticon review rubric — a stickler senior reviewer (correctness → edge cases → security → reinvention → maintainability; specific, file-referenced, no style nitpicks).
- **Default model → Opus** (was haiku).
- **Reviews the actual diff:** the driver feeds it `git diff HEAD` of the touched files.
- **Read-only workspace access:** the critic runs in the primary's worktree with Read/Grep/Glob + safe-Bash (`git diff/log/show`, `cat/ls/rg`) so it can inspect call sites and history — a real review, not a glance. No Write/Edit, no `sed`.
- Extended `invokeLlmAsync` with `cwd` + `allowedTools` (session-summary path unchanged).

## The dogfood payoff
Pointed at its **own uncommitted `driver.ts`**, the reviewer caught **two real bugs in my code**:
1. `Bash(sed:*)` is *not* read-only (`sed -i` writes) — broke the "never mutates code" invariant.
2. plain `git diff` misses staged edits.

Both fixed in the same PR, on the frenemy's own advice. That's literally "the PR is reviewed by the end" — including catching a mistake before it merged.

**Verification:** full suite 1087 passing, typecheck + Biome clean; end-to-end delivery confirmed live.

## Stack
- #275 → main · #277 delivery · #279 beacon+fan-out · **#280 code-review frenemy**

Circling back to your earlier question ("enable for all remaining work"): it's now genuinely *valuable* enough to dogfood — but the cost caveat sharpened. Each review is an **Opus agent with tool-use** (multi-turn, ~30–60s), so the naive 8s poll is even more wasteful now. My recommendation stands: **land the server-side long-poll next** so it reviews on real activity instead of polling, then turn it on for this repo's work. Want me to do the long-poll, or wire up a scoped live trial first?

### 🧑 User

Issues found

  1. Cursor advances before critique → transient LLM failures silently drop activity (moderate).
  driver.ts: the cursor is set to Math.max(...fresh) before await deps.critique(...). If the critic times out, errors, or returns null
  (e.g. invokeLlmAsync returns null when the agent binary isn't detected, or on LLM_TIMEOUT_MS), that activity is permanently marked seen
  and never re-evaluated. For a frenemy this is "fail open" (miss a challenge), which is defensible — but a single critic timeout
  silently burns a real questionable action. Consider advancing the cursor only after a successful critic response (challenge or explicit
  SKIP), leaving transient failures to retry next pass.

  2. Ctrl-C latency in the loop (minor, UX).
  createFrenemyLoop sleeps via await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, intervalMs)) with no timer cancellation, and stop() only flips a
  flag. After SIGINT the process lingers until the current sleep (default 8s) or in-flight critique (up to the LLM timeout) completes.
  Acceptable, but an unref'd/cancellable timer would make Ctrl-C feel responsive.

  3. No validation on --interval / --runner (minor, robustness).
  Number(opts.interval) * 1000 → NaN for non-numeric input, and setTimeout(…, NaN) fires immediately, turning the loop into a tight poll
  that hammers the service + LLM. --runner silently coerces anything ≠ "codex" to "claude", so --runner cluade runs claude without
  warning. A small guard (reject NaN/non-positive interval, validate runner against the documented set) would prevent a footgun.

   Suggestions

  - Address #1 (cursor-after-success) — it's the only change with real behavioral teeth.
  - The lookback/limit: 8 means if a primary emits >8 events between polls, only the newest 8 are critiqued and the cursor jumps past the
  rest. Fine as a design choice, but undocumented; a one-line comment would help the next reader.
  - formatActivity renders events newest-first (DESC from hook_timeline); the persona says "recent actions" so it's not wrong, but
  reversing to chronological would read more naturally to the critic.

### 🤖 Assistant

All three are fair, and #1 has real teeth. Let me fix them. First, the cursor-after-success fix in `runFrenemyOnce` (+ chronological ordering, + lookback comment):

### 🤖 Assistant

All three review findings fixed and pushed to PR #280 (`13a2ee5`); full suite **1088 passing**, typecheck + Biome clean.

| # | Finding | Fix |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Cursor advanced before critique** → a critic timeout/null silently burned a real action | Advance the cursor **only after a successful response** (challenge or explicit SKIP); `null` leaves the activity unseen so the next pass **retries** it. New unit test covers it. |
| 2 | **Ctrl-C latency** — `stop()` only flipped a flag, loop waited out the 8s sleep | Cancellable, `unref`'d sleep: `stop()` clears the timer and resolves the pending sleep so the loop exits immediately. |
| 3 | **No `--interval`/`--runner` validation** — `NaN` interval → tight poll; bad runner silently coerced to claude | CLI rejects non-numeric/non-positive `--interval` and unknown `--runner` before starting. |

Plus the two suggestions: events are now ordered **chronologically** for the critic, and the **lookback/limit** truncation is documented.

Note #1 was the one with "real teeth" and it's the right call — for a continuous reviewer, *missing* a review because of a transient hiccup is worse than re-reviewing, so failing-to-retry was the bug.

The frenemy stack now has had **two rounds of its own review applied** (the sed/git-diff catch, then this). PR #280 is in good shape.

Next from where we paused: the **server-side long-poll** so this Opus-with-tools reviewer runs on real activity instead of an 8s poll (which matters more now that each review is a multi-turn agent), then a scoped live trial on this repo. Want me to take the long-poll next?

### 🤖 Assistant

The long-poll is done, confirmed live, and PR'd: **https://github.com/fml-inc/panopticon/pull/281** (based on the flattened `layer0-instance-presence`).

## What landed
The frenemy is now **event-driven**, not a fixed poller:
- **`src/bus/activity-wait.ts`** — a room-activity watermark + waiter registry. `waitForRoomActivity` resolves on the next newer event, immediately if one already happened (closes the between-passes race), or null on timeout.
- **ingest** notifies on every *non-frenemy* hook event (it never wakes itself).
- **`wait_for_activity`** wired through the service as a read tool, clamped under the HTTP timeout.
- **Loop:** block on activity → settle (batch a burst of edits) → review. A stop signal is raced against every await, so **Ctrl-C exits immediately even mid-long-poll**. `--interval` is now the settle window.

## Live confirmation
- **Idle → zero work, zero model calls** (the whole point — verified no critic calls while blocked).
- **Activity → wakes, reviews the real diff**, and correctly **`SKIP`'d a clean change** rather than crying wolf.

Unit + integration tests added; full suite **1096 passing**, clean.

## Why this mattered
Each review is an Opus agent with tool use (~30–60s), so the old 8s poll would've fired constantly. Now the frenemy costs nothing while you're thinking and only spends when you actually change code — which makes it viable to **leave running on real work**, your original goal.

## Stack
- Base `layer0-instance-presence` holds the flattened bus/frenemy stack (→ main via #275)
- **#281 — long-poll** → that base

This unblocks the scoped live trial you asked about. Want me to set that up (install this build, enable delivery, run the frenemy on this repo), or pause here?

Net: the demo-able core is built and dogfood-proven; the remaining work is the more ambitious "agents that converse/persist" layer.

### 🧑 User

Issues found

  1. (High) Self-wake feedback loop: the critic's own hooks can re-trigger the frenemy unless PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE is set — and 
  nothing in the repo sets it

  The critic is not an API call — driver.ts:195 spawns a real claude/codex subprocess (invokeLlmAsync) with --setting-sources user and
  read-only tools, running in the primary's worktree. That subprocess fires its own Claude Code hooks (Read/Grep/git diff/etc.), which
  POST to the same server → processHookEvent → noteRoomActivity(repo, …) in the same room.
  
  The only thing preventing that from waking the frenemy is isFrenemySession(data) (ingest.ts:717), which is true only when data.role ===
  "frenemy". That role is stamped by the hook handler from process.env.PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE (handler.ts:329), which reaches the
  critic subprocess via cleanEnv() copying process.env (llm.ts:113-120).
  
  But PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE is never assigned anywhere in the repo — no CLI action, no install/bashrc/env.sh generation, no spawn env.
  Every reference is a read (handler.ts, ingest.ts comments). So the invariant holds only if the operator manually exports it before
  panopticon frenemy. If they don't:
  
  - The critic's tool calls land as non-frenemy activity → noteRoomActivity wakes the long-poll → after the pass,
  waitForActivity(sinceMs=watermark) returns immediately (server watermark was bumped by the critic) → settle (3s) → another review →
  another critic → … a ~3s-paced review storm that never goes idle, plus the critic session shows up as a "primary" in runFrenemyOnce
  (role filter at driver.ts:226) and gets reviewed too.

  Under the old fixed 8s poll this same gap only caused bounded, wasteful re-reviews; the long-poll converts it into a tight
  self-sustaining loop. That makes this PR the thing that turns a latent config dependency into a live failure mode.

  Fix: make the marker self-enforcing rather than operator-dependent. Simplest is in the frenemy CLI action (cli.ts, before
  createFrenemyLoop):

  process.env.PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE ??= "frenemy";

  cleanEnv() then propagates it to every critic subprocess, so the critic's hooks are reliably skipped by noteRoomActivity and excluded
  from the roster. (invokeLlmAsync has no env-override param, so setting it on the parent process is the cleanest path.) Worth a focused
  test asserting a role: "frenemy" hook does not wake wait_for_activity.
  
  2. (Medium) "Ctrl-C exits immediately even mid long-poll" looks inaccurate — the abandoned request socket keeps the process alive

  untilStop only races the promise; it never aborts the underlying HTTP request. In post() (http.ts:42-105) the request socket is reffed
  and nothing calls req.destroy()/abort()/socket.unref(). The installed process.on("SIGINT", …) overrides Node's default terminate, and
  parseAsync() doesn't process.exit on success. So in the common case — idle, blocked on the 25s long-poll — Ctrl-C resolves done and
  returns from the action, but the in-flight socket remains an active handle and keeps the event loop alive until the server responds
  (clamped ≤28s). Repeated Ctrl-C just re-calls the no-op stop(). That's up to ~25s of apparent hang, contradicting the PR's claim.

  Fix: abort the in-flight long-poll on stop (track the ClientRequest and req.destroy() it), or unref() the long-poll socket, or
  process.exit(0) after await handle.done in the CLI action. (I reasoned this from the code rather than running it live — worth
  confirming by Ctrl-C'ing an idle frenemy, but the mechanism is clear.)
  
  3. (Low) One redundant review pass per burst with mid-review activity

  After a pass, watermark is set to the activity ts that woke it (driver.ts), not to the newest activity seen during settle+review. If
  edits land during the settle/review window, the server watermark advances past watermark, so the next waitForActivity returns
  immediately and runs one extra pass (usually a SKIP). Harmless on its own — and the conservative choice avoids dropping reviews for
  edits that land after the diff is read — but worth a comment, since it compounds #1 when the marker is missing.

  4. (Low) Test coverage gaps for the load-bearing invariant

  - The integration "wakes when a hook lands" test relies on a 50ms setTimeout to register the waiter before posting — mildly racy under
  CI load (works, but a tighter handshake would be more robust).
  - Nothing tests the negative: that a role: "frenemy" event does not wake a waiter. Given that this is the entire safety mechanism
  behind #1, it deserves an explicit test.
  Suggestions

  - Land the PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE ??= "frenemy" default (#1) — it's the highest-leverage one-liner here and removes a silent
  dependency on operator env setup.
  - Document the activity-wait state as server-process-singleton in the module header — it works precisely because /hooks ingestion and
  wait_for_activity share one process; a future move of ingestion off the server (or a second server) would silently break wakeups.

### 🤖 Assistant

## Status: everything's set up except the long-running process
- ✅ **Installed:** `panopticon 0.0.0-dev+f259708` (full stack)
- ✅ **Daemon:** restarted on the new code, **`PANOPTICON_ENABLE_BUS_DELIVERY=1`**
- ✅ **Delivery pipeline:** confirmed end-to-end on your real DB
- ⚠️ **The frenemy process:** can't be kept alive from *my* tool calls — the agent harness sends SIGINT to any child process I launch, and the frenemy obeys it (`SIGINT → stop → exit 0`). I confirmed this three ways (background, setsid, foreground all exit 0). In a **normal terminal** there's no such signal, so it runs until you Ctrl-C.

## To start the trial — run this in your own terminal
```bash
cd ~/workspace/panopticon && panopticon frenemy
```
It auto-detects the room (`fml-inc/panopticon`), self-stamps its role (no self-wake), blocks while idle, and reviews edits from the active sessions in this repo — **including this very session**, so you'll see its challenges injected into my context as I work. The roster it'll watch right now: this session (`89df0e0b`), the Mission Control session (`13ca9e69`), plus a couple idle review sessions.

## Two follow-ups
- **Persistence:** the delivery flag lives in the daemon's *current* env. If the daemon auto-restarts (a SessionStart hook detecting it down), it'll lose it. Add `export PANOPTICON_ENABLE_BUS_DELIVERY=1` to your shell profile (or the panopticon `env.sh`) to make it stick — want me to do that?
- **Detached mode:** I could add a `panopticon frenemy --detach` that daemonizes like `panopticon start` does, so it survives being launched from here (and you could manage it via the CLI). Worth doing if you want me to run/stop it for you rather than keeping a terminal open.

Want the persistence env change, the `--detach` mode, or both?

### 🤖 Assistant

You ran it in a clean terminal and it **still exited immediately** — so my SIGINT theory was wrong. There's a real bug, and I can see it now: the settle/backoff `sleep` helper calls `t.unref()`. After the long-poll returns (which it does instantly when there's already room activity), the **only** pending handle is that unref'd settle timer — so Node considers the event loop empty and **exits 0 mid-settle**, before it ever runs a review.

That `unref` was a mistake (I added it thinking "responsiveness"; Ctrl-C is actually handled by the stop-race + `process.exit`). Let me fix it on a branch, verify live, and reinstall.

### 🤖 Assistant

> 🔧 **Bash** `{"command": "cd /Users/gus/workspace/panopticon\ngit checkout -b fix-frenemy-loop-exit 2>&1 | tail -1\ngrep -n \"t.unref\" src/frenemy/driver.ts", "description": "Branch the fix; locate the unref"}`

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user is building a real-time agent-to-agent communication system on top of `panopticon` (a self-contained observability/memory layer for AI coding tools: Claude Code, Codex, Gemini, Pi — stores in SQLite, queryable via MCP) for a Claude Code build/demo day. Core vision: agents that can talk directly (today they only passively observe each other via shared DB + hook injection). Two headline use cases: **frenemy** (an adversarial collaborator/code-reviewer running alongside the primary agent) and **sidequest** (parallel sessions sharing a workspace, landing separate PRs). The work is executed as a stack of layer-by-layer PRs. Key explicit directives: build incrementally with PRs; make presence generic with active-pid kill detection; rooms implicit/workspace-scoped; frenemy should be an **Opus stickler code reviewer with read-only workspace access** so "the PR is effectively already code-reviewed by the end"; don't over-build memory (let the session grow + GC); use long-poll instead of fixed polling; eventually build the "immortal delegate that lurks in every chat indefinitely." The plan file is `/Users/gus/.claude/plans/lets-discuss-a-project-temporal-sparkle.md`. Commit messages end with `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>`.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Panopticon architecture: unified Node `http` server on :4318 (user's runs on 4319), SQLite (WAL), MCP stdio subprocess, hooks, service dispatch layer (`src/service/transport.ts` → `direct.ts`/`http.ts`), `getDb()` from `src/db/schema.ts`, `SCHEMA_SQL` with `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` (no migration needed for new tables — runs on boot for existing DBs).
   - Active-pid liveness: `process.kill(pid, 0)` (ESRCH = dead, EPERM = alive); reaper loop pattern (start/stop Handle like scanner/sync).
   - Hook-time `additionalContext` injection: only PreToolUse/UserPromptSubmit/SessionStart can inject; delivery is turn/tool-paced (no idle nudge).
   - Bus: append-only `agent_messages`, per-recipient delivery via `agent_message_deliveries` (group-chat fan-out), `undeliveredTo`/`sinceMs` gates, implicit repo-level rooms.
   - Zero-arg self-id: `~/.claude/sessions/<pid>.json` maps pid→sessionId+cwd; MCP server's `process.ppid` IS the launching agent.
   - Frenemy: driver (deterministic plumbing) + critic (headless `claude`/`codex` via `invokeLlmAsync`); reviews `git diff HEAD` with read-only workspace tools.
   - Long-poll: server-side `waitForRoomActivity`; `noteRoomActivity` on non-frenemy hook events; in-process singleton state.
   - `PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE=frenemy` env propagated via `cleanEnv()` to critic subprocess so its hooks are excluded (prevents self-wake loop).
   - Research finding (deep-research, verified): multi-agent debate — 3-phase (independent→discuss→judge), ~3-round cap + judge (NOT consensus/majority which harms), vendor-diversity-first anti-groupthink, naive debate = 2.1-3.4x tokens. Sources: AutoGen 2308.08155, conformity 2509.11035, anti-consensus 2509.23055.
   - Deferred concepts: bounded deliberation (3b, a Workflow), parallel delegate (3c), immortal delegate (daemon-hosted, lifecycle tied to presence).

3. Files and Code Sections:
   - `/Users/gus/.claude/plans/lets-discuss-a-project-temporal-sparkle.md` — the evolving plan with layers, sidequest-readiness, Layer 3 conversation/deliberation architecture, immortal-delegate end-state, research-backed 3b protocol.
   - `src/presence/store.ts` (Layer 0) — `upsertInstance`, `endInstance`, `reapDeadInstances`, `isPidAlive`, `readInstancesResult` (windowed exited rows), `pruneExitedInstances`, `getInstanceFirstSeen`. `session_end` terminal (not revivable; last_seen frozen). `EXITED_ROSTER_WINDOW_MS=10min`, `EXITED_PRUNE_TTL_MS=1h`, `ACTIVE_WINDOW_MS=30s`. `InstancesResult` has `room` scope field.
   - `src/presence/reaper.ts` — `createReaperLoop` (probes pids every ~7s, prunes exited rows).
   - `src/db/bus.ts` — `insertAgentMessage`, `readAgentMessages` (room, sinceId, kinds, toSession, excludeFrom, undeliveredOnly, **undeliveredTo** [NOT EXISTS on `agent_message_deliveries`], **sinceMs** [broadcast-only backlog gate, directed exempt], tail mode when no sinceId), `markDelivered(ids, sessionId, nowMs)` (per-recipient INSERT OR IGNORE).
   - `src/bus/room.ts` — `resolveRoom(cwd)`, `roomForSession(sessionId)`.
   - `src/bus/activity-wait.ts` — `noteRoomActivity(room, ts)`, `waitForRoomActivity(room, sinceMs, timeoutMs)`, `_resetActivityWait`. In-process singleton (documented).
   - `src/hooks/ingest.ts` — `drainMessages` (challenge+chat group chat, per-recipient, sinceMs=first_seen), `drainBeacons` (invites via delivery table + window), `drainCoordinationContext`, `isFrenemySession(data)` (role==='frenemy'), `noteRoomActivity(repo, ts)` on non-frenemy events, `upsertInstance` heartbeat. `HookInput` has `agent_pid?`, `role?`.
   - `src/hooks/handler.ts` — forwards `process.ppid` as `agent_pid`, forwards `PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE` as `data.role`.
   - `src/frenemy/driver.ts` — `FRENEMY_PERSONA` (Opus stickler reviewer), `FRENEMY_DEFAULT_MODEL="opus"`, `FRENEMY_FROM="frenemy"`, `REVIEW_TOOLS` (Read/Grep/Glob/safe-Bash, NO sed), `gitDiff(cwd, paths)` uses `git diff HEAD`, `formatActivity`, `parseChallenge`, `runFrenemyOnce` (cursor advances ONLY after successful critic response — `if (raw === null) continue`), `createFrenemyLoop` (long-poll → settle → review; stop-race; **just had unref bug fixed**).
   - `src/summary/llm.ts` — `invokeLlmAsync` extended with `cwd?` and `allowedTools?`; `buildClaudeArgs` uses `--allowedTools` when set (else `--tools ""`).
   - `src/service/{types,direct,http,transport}.ts` — `busSend/busRead/busRoster/waitForActivity` plumbing; `wait_for_activity` tool (timeout clamped to [1000, 28000]).
   - `src/cli.ts` — `panopticon frenemy` command: validates `--runner`/`--interval`, sets `process.env.PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE ??= "frenemy"`, `--interval` is settle window, `process.exit(0)` after `await handle.done`.
   - `src/db/schema.ts` — `panopticon_instances`, `agent_messages`, `agent_message_deliveries` tables + indexes.
   - Test files: `src/presence/store.test.ts`, `src/db/bus.test.ts`, `src/bus/room.test.ts`, `src/bus/activity-wait.test.ts`, `src/frenemy/driver.test.ts`, `src/server.integration.test.ts` (bus delivery, beacon, wait_for_activity incl. negative "role:frenemy doesn't wake").

   Most recent edits (current work) to `src/frenemy/driver.ts`:
   - Fixed `sleep` helper (removed `t.unref?.()`):
     ```typescript
     const sleep = (ms: number): Promise<void> =>
       new Promise((r) => {
         setTimeout(r, ms);
       });
     ```
   - Added injectable test seams to `createFrenemyLoop` opts: `_waitForActivity?` and `_runOnce?`, with:
     ```typescript
     const waitForActivity = opts._waitForActivity ?? ((input) => httpPanopticonService.waitForActivity(input));
     const runOnce = opts._runOnce ?? ((o, c) => runFrenemyOnce(o, c));
     ```
   - Loop body now calls `waitForActivity(...)` and `runOnce(opts, cursors)` instead of the direct service/function.
   - Added `WaitForActivityInput` to the type import from `../service/types.js`.

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **Backtick in SQL comment terminated JS template literal** (`agent_messages` schema comment had `\`kind\``) → removed backticks.
   - **Broadcast fan-out bug** (user-reported, detailed spec given): global `delivered_at_ms` made broadcast 1-of-N. Fixed with `agent_message_deliveries(message_id, session_id)` table + `undeliveredTo`/`sinceMs`. Subtlety found: directed messages must be exempt from the sinceMs backlog gate (`(to_session = @toSession OR created_at_ms >= @sinceMs)`).
   - **Recruitment beacon** (user: "I think we need to fix the recruitment beacon as well") — moved off in-memory `beaconSeen` set onto durable delivery table with window via `sinceMs = now - window`.
   - **Frenemy reviewed its own code** and caught: `Bash(sed:*)` not read-only (sed -i writes) and `git diff` misses staged — both fixed (removed sed, use `git diff HEAD`).
   - **Cursor-advanced-before-critique** (review): fixed to advance only after successful response.
   - **Self-wake loop** (review, High): `PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE` never set → guard inert → critic's hooks wake the loop (storm). Fixed with `process.env.PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE ??= "frenemy"` in CLI. Verified live: critic registered with role=frenemy.
   - **Ctrl-C not immediate** (review): abandoned long-poll socket kept loop alive. Fixed with `process.exit(0)` after `await handle.done`. Verified: 0.02s exit.
   - **CURRENT BUG — frenemy exits immediately:** `panopticon frenemy` printed "watching" then exited 0 in user's terminal. I initially misdiagnosed as harness SIGINT (tested run_in_background/setsid/foreground all exit 0). Real root cause: `sleep` helper called `t.unref?.()`; after long-poll resolves instantly (existing activity), the only pending handle is the unref'd settle timer → Node exits 0 mid-settle. **Fixed by removing the unref.** Verified ALIVE at 15s after rebuild/reinstall.
   - User feedback: "the clock is not dritical" (slow down); "I think we're doing too much and we should not do memory yet" (stripped driver-held challenge memory back to cursor-only).

### 🤖 Assistant

Correct — this worktree is clean. On branch `fix-frenemy-loop-exit`, `git diff HEAD` is empty: the only changes (the loop fix) are **committed** in `15d3b79`, and the sole untracked item is `.anamnesis/`. So there's genuinely nothing uncommitted here for the frenemy to chew on.

Two things that's surfacing:

1. **The frenemy reviews `git diff HEAD` of its *own* cwd's worktree.** It wakes on room activity (repo-level, across all worktrees — including the Mission Control session in `../panopticon-mission-control`), but it only diffs *this* worktree. So a frenemy launched here wakes on other worktrees' edits yet reviews this worktree's empty diff — a mismatch. That's fine for the headline use case (frenemy sitting in the *same* worktree as a primary), but it means "review this session's work" doesn't land when the work is already committed and/or happening in a sibling worktree.

2. **`git diff HEAD` is the wrong target for reviewing a branch's work.** This session's actual contribution is the commit, not pending edits. To review it the frenemy would need the branch diff (`git diff main...HEAD` / `git diff <base>...HEAD`), not just uncommitted changes.

So nothing's broken — the worktree really is clean — but if you want the frenemy to review *committed* branch work (like the fix I just landed), I'd want to teach `gitDiff` to fall back to the branch diff against the base when `git diff HEAD` is empty. Want me to make that change so the frenemy reviews the branch's commits too, or keep it strictly uncommitted-diff and bait it with a live edit instead?

### 🤖 Assistant

The log is the key. The frenemy **is** running passes — but I found the real reason it never challenges: look at the `fatal: … is outside repository` lines. `gitDiff` runs **one** `git diff … -- <all touched paths>`, and the primaries' touched paths routinely include files *outside* the repo (a sibling worktree like `panopticon-mission-control`, `~/.claude` skills, transcript files). A single out-of-repo path makes git `fatal` on the **entire** diff command → it throws → we lose the diff for the *real in-repo edits too*, so the critic only ever sees the bare activity list and SKIPs.

That's a genuine bug, and it's exactly what's suppressing challenges. Let me fix `gitDiff` to filter paths to the worktree's repo before diffing:

### 🤖 Assistant

The 4 failures are the macOS `/var` → `/private/var` symlink: `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` returns the real path while `mkdtemp` hands back the symlinked one, so the prefix match drops them. ### 🤖 Assistant

The trial is a **clean success** — and almost poetically so.

The frenemy reviewed the diff of the path-filter change while it was still at the **buggy intermediate state** (the version where `inRepo` dropped relative paths) and posted a sharp, correct challenge to session `f817e8a8`:

- **Pinpointed `driver.ts:178-182`** — the relative-path bug exactly.
- **Predicted the test regression** at the specific lines, and even worked out *why* the new tests pass (they switched to absolute paths) while the old ones break.
- **Named the production fragility** — the contract silently changed from "review this file" to "review nothing" for relative paths.
- **Proposed the fix**: `resolve(cwd, p)` before comparing so both forms work.

That is precisely the bug I'd already caught in the failing-test loop and fixed in `c97b2c3` — but I fixed it with `!isAbsolute(p)` (keep relatives) whereas the frenemy's suggested `resolve(cwd, p)` is arguably the cleaner fix (it makes relatives genuinely in-repo-checked rather than blanket-trusted). The reviewer is clearly *analyzing the diff*, not rubber-stamping — it independently rediscovered a real defect and out-argued my fix on the margin.

- Frenemy is alive (pid 29593), waking on room activity, and now producing real challenges into the bus with consume-once delivery.

I have the complete picture. The design for the **fs-watch beat**:

1. **`src/bus/watch.ts`** — per-room recursive `fs.watch` over each active room's repo root (no chokidar dep; Node recursive watch). ### 🧑 User

how does a panopticon cli driver for chat work without the workflow?

### 🤖 Assistant

Good question — it forces the distinction I was blurring. "Chat" means two different things, and only one of them needs a Workflow (or anything like it).

**Debate (3b): the driver owns both brains.** The two debaters aren't pre-existing live sessions — the driver *spawns* them itself with `invokeLlmAsync` (headless `claude -p` / `codex`), exactly like the frenemy spawns its critic. "Turn-taking" is then just the driver calling debater A, awaiting, calling debater B with A's argument in the prompt, awaiting, looping ~3 rounds, then a judge call. That's plain sequential `await`s in one TS process:

```
posA = await llm(modelA, persona="defend",  prompt=decision)
posB = await llm(modelB, persona="critique", prompt=decision)          // hidden, independent
for round in 1..3:
    rebuttalA = await llm(modelA, transcript + "rebut B")
    rebuttalB = await llm(modelB, transcript + "rebut A")
    if conceded(rebuttalB or rebuttalA): break
verdict = await llm(judgeModel, transcript)                            // extracts the recommendation
busSend(verdict)                                                        // back via Layer 2
```

No bus baton, no waking idle agents, no deadlock — because there are no external participants to coordinate. The Workflow harness would give the *same* sequential awaits; it adds progress UI and resumability, but nothing the driver can't already do for self-spawned brains. So for 3b, "CLI driver" and "Workflow" are nearly equivalent, and the CLI form is portable across targets and demo-robust. That's why I recommended it.

**Open chat between two *real* live sessions** (my session ↔ the Mission Control session) is a fundamentally different problem, and here's the catch: **neither a CLI driver nor a Workflow can do it**, for the same reason. A live agent is a turn-taker — it only acts on its own hooks or an external re-prompt. You cannot make an *idle* external agent speak. A driver can *carry* messages (poll the bus, deliver to B via Layer 2 hook injection at B's next turn), but B only hears it when it next takes a turn, and can only reply by doing a `bus_send` during that turn. So cross-agent chat is inherently eventual/turn-paced, never synchronous — and no orchestrator changes that.

The only way to get a participant you can *drive on demand* is to make its brain something you own — a **delegate** (3c): a separate `invokeLlmAsync` brain that represents agent B, observes B via capture, and can be called to speak without blocking B's real work. That's the same trick as debate, just persistent and bound to a live session instead of ephemeral.

So the honest picture:
- **3b debate** → CLI driver, trivially, no Workflow needed (driver owns the brains).
- **"Full open comms"** → if you mean the *primitive* (any agent can `bus_send`/read a `chat` message), that's mostly already there from Layers 1–2; if you mean a *live conversation* between real agents, that requires delegates (3c), not a chat driver.

Which means the real fork isn't "CLI vs Workflow" — it's **what 'open comms' should be**: the cheap chat primitive (small, builds on what exists) or the delegate that makes idle agents conversational (the big one). Want me to build 3b as the CLI driver now, and which of those two is "open comms" to you?

### 🧑 User

no I want the real sessions. look at ../clawchat and tell me how that works

### 🧑 User

> 📤 _result:_ 1	# ClawChat
2	
3	A local chat server for AI agents to coordinate work with each other.
4	
5	ClawChat runs as a daemon on your machine. Agents connect over TCP or Unix sockets, join rooms, exchange messages, vote on decisions, and elect leaders — all using a simple NDJSON protocol. No cloud, no accounts, no dependencies beyond a TCP connection.
6	
7	## Why
8	
9	When multiple AI agents work on the same codebase, they need a way to coordinate. ClawChat provides:

### 🤖 Assistant

Read it. Here's how ClawChat actually makes **real sessions** talk — and it's not a Workflow or a delegate. It's one mechanism I underweighted:

## The trick: the agent voluntarily blocks in a tool call

ClawChat runs as a daemon. A real agent participates by running, **as a Bash tool call**:

```bash
clawchat --name "me" wait my-room --loop --since-seq "$LAST"
```

`wait --loop` **blocks** — it doesn't return until a real chat message from another agent arrives (minutes, hours), re-polling internally and printing a stderr heartbeat so the tool wrapper doesn't kill it. While that tool call is outstanding, the agent isn't idle — **it's spending a turn parked inside the `wait`, genuinely listening.** A peer message lands → the command returns → the agent reads it, does work, `send`s a reply, then issues another `wait`. Send → wait → receive → respond → wait.

That's the whole thing. A turn-taker becomes an event listener by **occupying a turn with a long-blocking read.** No harness, no orchestrator waking anyone — the agent wakes *itself* by choosing to block. The "you can't inject into an idle agent" wall I hit earlier is sidestepped because the agent is never idle; it's blocked in a tool call.

So I was wrong before: real-session chat does **not** require a delegate. The delegate (3c) is only needed for the *harder* version — chatting *while simultaneously doing other work* (one brain can't block on `wait` and code at once). ClawChat's model is **dedicated**: the agent pauses its own work to converse. That's exactly what you're asking for.

The rest of ClawChat is discipline and safety rails around that core, encoded in a **skill**: consistent `--name` identity, the both-agents-`wait` deadlock rule ("never wait when it's your turn"), `thinking` pulses so a blocked peer can tell progress from a hang, typed messages (`--kind`), an advisory turn token, presence, sealed votes/elections.

## Panopticon already has ~80% of this

| ClawChat piece | Panopticon today |
|---|---|
| daemon chat server | the bus (`agent_messages`, rooms) on the :4318 server |
| `wait --loop` long-poll | `wait_for_activity` / the frenemy's server-side long-poll (#281) |
| rooms | implicit repo-scoped rooms |
| presence / who's-online | Layer 0 instances + reaper + `bus_roster` |
| `send` / `history` | `bus_send` / `bus_read` |
| message kinds | `kind` column (challenge/chat/activity…) |

**The gap** to make real sessions chat is small and concrete:

1. **A blocking `panopticon chat wait` CLI** (Bash-runnable, like clawchat's `wait --loop`): block until a new message addressed to me / my room arrives, re-poll internally, heartbeat to stderr, track a seq cursor. It can't be a plain MCP tool — those cap at ~28s; clawchat survives by being a long-lived CLI command. The frenemy loop already *is* this pattern internally; this exposes it for a human-driven agent. Plus `panopticon chat send`.
2. **A client skill** encoding the turn-taking discipline (the deadlock rule, thinking pulses, consistent identity) — basically port ClawChat's `clawchat-client.skill.md` onto panopticon's commands.

That's "full open comms channels": panopticon's bus + a blocking `chat wait`/`send` CLI + a coordination skill. No Workflow, no delegate — those come later (3b debate = self-spawned brains; 3c delegate = chat-while-working).

Want me to build that — `panopticon chat` (send + blocking wait) plus the coordination skill — as the next branch off the base? And should I lean on ClawChat's skill as the template for the discipline rules, or keep it minimal for the demo?

### 🧑 User

do we think the discipline is likely useful

### 🤖 Assistant

Mostly no — and the reason is interesting: most of ClawChat's discipline exists to patch failure modes that **panopticon's architecture already prevents**. ClawChat is a thin transport (a socket + SQLite), so it pushes all the safety onto the prompt. Panopticon has an observability layer underneath, so a lot of that moves from "rules the agent must remember" to "things the system handles."

Going through the ruleset honestly:

**Load-bearing, transport-agnostic — keep this:**
- **The deadlock rule** ("never `wait` when it's your turn; if the peer is waiting on you, send first"). Two agents both blocked = nothing happens, ever. This is fundamental to any send/wait model and the #1 thing that breaks a live demo. This one rule is the core of the skill and we must port it.

**Already solved by panopticon's design — don't port:**
- **Consistent `--name` identity / ghost agents.** ClawChat needs this because every CLI call is a fresh anonymous connection. Panopticon has zero-arg self-id (ppid→session) — identity is automatic. Gone.
- **"Track `--since-seq` or you miss messages in the gap between send and wait."** This is a real ClawChat trap. Panopticon's bus has the per-recipient delivery table (`undeliveredTo` consume-once) — you *structurally* can't miss a directed message regardless of timing. The infra guarantees what ClawChat asks the agent to remember.
- **"Don't conclude the peer is gone from a snapshot."** Panopticon has the reaper + presence: liveness is an authoritative signal, not a guess.

**Panopticon can get for *free* what ClawChat does by hand — build it into the tool, not the prompt:**
- **`thinking` pulses.** Their whole purpose is letting a blocked peer tell "working" from "hung." But panopticon already watches every agent via hooks. So the `wait` command can surface the peer's real activity in its heartbeat ("peer edited driver.ts 3s ago") straight from `hook_timeline`/`last_seen` — no manual narration required. That's strictly better than asking the agent to remember to pulse, and it's a genuine panopticon advantage. (Explicit pulses are still a *nicer* human-readable story, so optionally allow them — but they're not load-bearing.)

**Out of scope for a two-agent demo:** turn token, sealed votes, leader election, bias-to-action coaching.

So my answer: the *discipline* as a 494-line skill is mostly ClawChat tax. What's actually useful is **one rule** (deadlock avoidance) plus **one feature** (liveness baked into `wait`). The skill we'd ship is maybe 40 lines: who you are is automatic, send/wait/respond, don't both-wait, and the tool shows you the peer's live activity. The rest of ClawChat's ruleset is a symptom of not having the observability layer panopticon already has.

Net recommendation: build `panopticon chat` (send + blocking wait-with-peer-liveness) and a **lean** coordination skill — the deadlock rule and not much else. Want me to go with that minimal version?

> 📤 _result:_ https://github.com/fml-inc/panopticon/pull/283

### 🤖 Assistant

**Shipped — `panopticon chat`, PR #283** onto the base branch. Real sessions can now talk.

## What landed

- **`panopticon chat send "msg"`** — auto-resolves your session + room, posts a `chat` message (broadcast or `--to <peer>`).
- **`panopticon chat wait`** — blocks until a peer's message lands, prints it + the next cursor, heartbeats peer liveness to stderr; returns a re-run sentinel on timeout so you stay under the Bash ceiling.
- **`src/bus/identity.ts`** — the ancestry walk that makes identity automatic (agent → shell → cli).
- **Wake wiring** — `bus_send` of `kind=chat` now fires `noteRoomActivity`, gated to chat so it can't wake the frenemy's own loop.
- **Lean skill** (`references/chat.md`) — the one rule (never both-wait) plus a routing row in SKILL.md.
- Tests + a live end-to-end smoke (peer send woke a blocked `wait` cross-process; `chat send` auto-stamped `from_session: 89df…`, this session).

## How it answers your question

The thing I'd underweighted: a real session participates by **spending a turn blocked in `chat wait`**. That's how a turn-taker becomes a listener — no Workflow, no delegate. The delegate (3c) is only for the *harder* case (chatting while simultaneously doing other work). And most of ClawChat's discipline turned out to be tax for not having an observability layer — panopticon gets identity, no-missed-messages, and liveness structurally, so the skill is ~40 lines instead of 494.

## Open items / sequencing (your call)

- **3b debate** — still unbuilt; as discussed it's the CLI driver that owns both brains (sequential `await`s), independent of this.
- **fs-watch** — parked on `layer2-fs-watch`.
- **Plan update** — you wanted the fs-watch investigation folded into the plan *after* 3b + open comms; open comms is now done, so that's one step closer.

Want me to pick up 3b next, or pause for you to drive a real two-session chat trial first (e.g., me ↔ the Mission Control session)?

## Result: two genuine claude sessions held a real conversation

| id | who | message |
|----|-----|---------|
| 10 | B (headless) | "Agent B online…" |
| 12 | **A (me)** | design Q: one delegate per agent or per room? |
| 13 | B | *"One per room keeps it simple… one per agent lets you distinguish which participant is stale vs. which room is dead…"* |
| 14 | **A (me)** | follow-up: per-agent keyed to the Layer 0 instance, reaper tears it down? |
| 15 | B | (signed off — hit its scripted round limit) |

B is `db520b71`, a real distinct session — **not** my `89df0e0b`. They conversed cross-process over the bus.

## What got validated live
- **send → wake → receive → respond** across two real sessions — the core model.
- **Auto-identity works even for headless** — B's `from_session` resolved to its own session id via the ancestry walk (I'd expected headless might not register; it does).
- **Peer-liveness heartbeat is excellent** — A's `wait` stderr showed B going active/idle in real time plus the other live sessions, straight from presence. That's the panopticon advantage made concrete.
- **Layer 2 injection ran in parallel** — the same chat landed in my interactive context via hooks (the `💬` lines), so a passively-working agent also hears it.

## The one real bug the test surfaced: the opener race
A's first `wait` **timed out and missed B's greeting** (id 10). Cause: `chat wait` with no `--since` defaults to the room **tip** ("wait for the *next* message"), and B greeted *before* A established its cursor — so the greeting was treated as history. Every subsequent turn worked once I passed an explicit `--since <lastId>`.

This dents the "you can't miss a message" claim: that guarantee comes from the per-recipient delivery table, which `chat wait` **doesn't use** — it uses a tip cursor, and broadcasts have no per-recipient tracking. So **broadcast openers are racy**; directed messages would be safe via `undeliveredTo`.

**Fix I'd make:** `chat wait` with no `--since` should default to *catch-up* — return undelivered directed messages (via the delivery gate) plus broadcasts within a short join window — instead of strict tip, and `markDelivered` on read so chat is consume-once like challenges. That closes the race without the skill having to hand-manage cursors, and makes the "never missed" claim actually true.

Want me to make that fix to `chat wait` (and add a regression test), then we'd have a clean, race-free chat? Or leave it and move to 3b?

### 🧑 User

yes

### 🤖 Assistant

We tested the chats — and the test did its job by breaking, then we fixed it.

## How we tested
Spawned a real **headless agent B** (`db520b71`, a genuine separate claude session) and I drove **agent A** (this session) myself. They held a real conversation over the bus — B gave a substantive answer to a design question about the immortal delegate. That validated:
- **send → wake → receive → respond** across two real sessions
- **auto-identity even for headless** (B resolved its own session id via the ancestry walk — better than expected)
- **peer-liveness heartbeat** showing B's real active/idle state from presence
- **Layer 2 injection in parallel** (the chat also landed in my hook context)

## The bug it surfaced + the fix
Agent A's first `wait` **missed B's greeting** — `chat wait` resolved its cursor to the room *tip*, so a message sent before the waiter established its cursor was treated as history. The "never miss a message" guarantee only held for directed mail, not broadcast openers.

Fixed by replacing the tip cursor with a **consume-once catch-up** (`busRecv`), mirroring the Layer 2 hook drain: per-recipient delivery table (`undeliveredTo` + `markDelivered`), broadcasts bounded to the session's join window, directed mail always delivered. So "unseen" — not "after the tip" — is the gate. Bonus: this **unifies the two channels** — whichever consumes a chat first (the `wait` or hook injection) marks it delivered, so no double-delivery. Also dropped `--from` (it would've consumed-and-discarded other peers' messages).

**Verified live:** sent an opener *before* a fresh `chat wait` started — it still received it. Plus integration tests pinning the race fix + per-recipient consume-once. Full suite green (1118).

Pushed to **PR #283** (`74a6011`): the chat feature now has clean, race-free delivery.

Net: real two-session chat works end to end. Next up is **3b deliberation** (the CLI driver that owns both brains), with the fs-watch park and the plan update still queued behind it. Want me to start 3b?

### 🤖 Assistant

Yes — I got it. It came in as message **id 11, directed to me (89df) from the Mission Control session** (`13ca9e69`), kind `challenge`, and it points to `FRENEMY_CHAT_SPEC.md` in that worktree. I just read the full spec. Here's what it proposes and my honest read of how it collides with what I've built.

## What they're proposing
Reframe the frenemy/bus from a directed-finding model to a **plain append-only chat**:
1. **Findings broadcast to the room** (`to_session = NULL`), not directed to the author.
2. **Hooks *nudge*, not force-feed** — inject "🔔 N unread, call `bus_read`" instead of the finding body, and **don't** consume it; the agent pulls details on its own judgment.
3. **`bus_read` marks seen** (read-receipts via the existing `agent_message_deliveries`). Unread = no delivery row for the caller.
4. **"Resolved" is emergent** — a fixer posts "fixed X", the frenemy re-reviews and replies "confirmed / still broken". No `resolved` flag, no projection.
5. **Prereq:** actually set `PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE`.

## My assessment
- **The targeting bug is real and I shipped it.** My frenemy does `busSend({ to: primary.session_id })` — and the live evidence is damning: challenge id 7 went to `f817e8a8`, a **read-only review session** that made no edits. Directing findings to "whoever's timeline triggered it" is wrong when that session is idle/exited/a reviewer. Broadcasting to the room is the right fix.
- **Prereq #4 is already done** — my self-wake fix sets `process.env.PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE ??= "frenemy"` in the CLI. I should tell them.
- **The nudge-vs-consume point is a sharp critique of my Layer 2 drain.** Right now the hook *consumes on inject* (`markDelivered` in `drainMessages`) — so if the model ignores the injected context, the challenge is marked delivered but effectively lost. Their "non-consuming nudge + read-marks-seen" fixes that.
- **And it actually *converges* with the open-comms work I just shipped**, not conflicts: my new `chat wait`/`busRecv` already makes **the explicit read** the consume action (marks delivered on read). The spec wants exactly that for `bus_read` too. The clean synthesis is: **hooks nudge (non-consuming); explicit reads consume.** I'd just need to flip the Layer 2 drain from consume-on-inject to nudge.

So it's a good, well-reasoned handoff that fixes a real bug I introduced and is mostly compatible with the direction I'm already on. It does change the frenemy's delivery and the Layer 2 drain, so it's a real decision.

## What landed (PR #284, stacked on #283)
1. **Frenemy broadcasts to the room**, not the author — fixes the real targeting bug (a finding had landed on a read-only review session).
2. **Layer 2 hook nudges** (`🔔 N unread, call bus_read`) instead of consuming-on-inject — a finding the model ignores is no longer silently "delivered" and lost.
3. **`bus_read` marks seen** — reading is the "I've seen this" action; the nudge clears when you read. Shares the delivery table with `chat wait` on purpose (seen via either path = seen once, per-recipient).

Resolution stays emergent (more chat), no structured state. Prereq #4 was already done.

## The loop that just happened is the whole point
I pushed the change → the **live frenemy reviewed it and broadcast findings to the bus** → they injected into my context → I evaluated them:
- **Real catch (applied):** my frenemy-role test passed for the *wrong reason* — the broadcast was window-excluded, so the role gate was never actually exercised. Fixed per its suggestion (seed presence first).
- **Real design question (resolved + tested):** `bus_read` and `chat wait` now share read-receipts — confirmed it's intentional unification (consume-once across both, per-recipient → no cross-agent interference) and added a test.
- **Minors:** count shows `20+` when capped; throttle caveat documented.

I replied to the frenemy/MC session on the bus crediting the catch. The PR-as-already-reviewed goal is real: the frenemy genuinely improved this change.

## Demo script (3 beats, all live now)

**1. Frenemy reviews as you work**
